     395             :  *
     396             :  * \brief Assign spatial reference to this object.
     397             :  *
     398             :  * Any existing spatial reference
     399             :  * is replaced, but under no circumstances does this result in the object
     400             :  * being reprojected.  It is just changing the interpretation of the existing
     401             :  * geometry.  Note that assigning a spatial reference increments the
     402             :  * reference count on the OGRSpatialReference, but does not copy it.
     403             :  *
     404             :  * Starting with GDAL 2.3, this will also assign the spatial reference to
     405             :  * potential sub-geometries of the geometry (OGRGeometryCollection,
     406             :  * OGRCurvePolygon/OGRPolygon, OGRCompoundCurve, OGRPolyhedralSurface and their
     407             :  * derived classes).

     409             :  * This is similar to the SFCOM IGeometry::put_SpatialReference() method.
     410             :  *

     676             : /**
     677             :  * \fn OGRErr OGRGeometry::transform( OGRCoordinateTransformation *poCT );
     678             :  *
     679             :  * \brief Apply arbitrary coordinate transformation to geometry.
     680             :  *
     681             :  * This method will transform the coordinates of a geometry from
     682             :  * their current spatial reference system to a new target spatial
     683             :  * reference system.  Normally this means reprojecting the vectors,
     684             :  * but it could include datum shifts, and changes of units.
     685             :  *
     686             :  * Note that this method does not require that the geometry already
     687             :  * have a spatial reference system.  It will be assumed that they can
     688             :  * be treated as having the source spatial reference system of the
     689             :  * OGRCoordinateTransformation object, and the actual SRS of the geometry
     690             :  * will be ignored.  On successful completion the output OGRSpatialReference
     691             :  * of the OGRCoordinateTransformation will be assigned to the geometry.
     692             :  *
     693             :  * This method is the same as the C function OGR_G_Transform().
     694             :  *
     695             :  * @param poCT the transformation to apply.
     696             :  *
     697             :  * @return OGRERR_NONE on success or an error code.
     698             :  */
     699             :

    3862             : /************************************************************************/
    3863             : /*                               Buffer()                               */
    3864             : /************************************************************************/
    3865             : 
    3866             : /**
    3867             :  * \brief Compute buffer of geometry.
    3868             :  *
    3869             :  * Builds a new geometry containing the buffer region around the geometry
    3870             :  * on which it is invoked.  The buffer is a polygon containing the region within
    3871             :  * the buffer distance of the original geometry.
    3872             :  *
    3873             :  * Some buffer sections are properly described as curves, but are converted to
    3874             :  * approximate polygons.  The nQuadSegs parameter can be used to control how
    3875             :  * many segments should be used to define a 90 degree curve - a quadrant of a
    3876             :  * circle.  A value of 30 is a reasonable default.  Large values result in
    3877             :  * large numbers of vertices in the resulting buffer geometry while small
    3878             :  * numbers reduce the accuracy of the result.
    3879             :  *
    3880             :  * This method is the same as the C function OGR_G_Buffer().
    3881             :  *
    3882             :  * This method is built on the GEOS library, check it for the definition
    3883             :  * of the geometry operation.
    3884             :  * If OGR is built without the GEOS library, this method will always fail,
    3885             :  * issuing a CPLE_NotSupported error.
    3886             :  *
    3887             :  * @param dfDist the buffer distance to be applied. Should be expressed into
    3888             :  *               the same unit as the coordinates of the geometry.
    3889             :  *
    3890             :  * @param nQuadSegs the number of segments used to approximate a 90
    3891             :  * degree (quadrant) of curvature.
    3892             :  *
    3893             :  * @return the newly created geometry, or NULL if an error occurs.
    3894             :  */
    3895             : 
    3896           7 : OGRGeometry *OGRGeometry::Buffer( UNUSED_IF_NO_GEOS double dfDist,
    3897             :                                   UNUSED_IF_NO_GEOS int nQuadSegs ) const
    3898             : 
    3899             : {
    3900             : #ifndef HAVE_GEOS
    3901             : 
    3902             :     CPLError( CE_Failure, CPLE_NotSupported,
    3903             :               "GEOS support not enabled." );
    3904             :     return nullptr;
    3905             : 
    3906             : #else
    3907             : 
    3908           7 :     OGRGeometry *poOGRProduct = nullptr;
    3909             : 
    3910           7 :     GEOSContextHandle_t hGEOSCtxt = createGEOSContext();
    3911           7 :     GEOSGeom hGeosGeom = exportToGEOS(hGEOSCtxt);
    3912           7 :     if( hGeosGeom != nullptr )
    3913             :     {
    3914             :         GEOSGeom hGeosProduct =
    3915           7 :             GEOSBuffer_r( hGEOSCtxt, hGeosGeom, dfDist, nQuadSegs );
